  <div id="readme" class="Box-body readme blob instapaper_body js-code-block-container">
    <article class="markdown-body entry-content p-3 p-md-6" itemprop="text"><h1><a id="user-content-comp6771---advanced-c-programming" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#comp6771---advanced-c-programming"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>COMP6771 - Advanced C++ Programming</h1>
<h2><a id="user-content-week-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#week-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Week 1</h2>
<h3><a id="user-content-style" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#style"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Style</h3>
<ul>
<li>NO Macros</li>
<li>Variables should be defined close to their use</li>
<li>Don't use <code>malloc/realloc</code>, use <code>new</code></li>
<li>Minimise use of pointer arithmetic</li>
<li>Place declarations in .h header files</li>
<li>Place definitions in .cpp source files</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-c-standard-library-stl" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#c-standard-library-stl"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>C++ Standard Library (STL)</h3>
<ul>
<li>The Standard Template Library (STL) is part of the C++ standard library</li>
<li>A generic (or reusable) library for managing collections of data with modern and efficient algorithms
<ul>
<li>Contianers: vector, list, stack</li>
<li>Algorithms, find, sort, copy</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-compiling" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#compiling"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Compiling</h3>
<ul>
<li>The compilation process:
<ul>
<li>Preprocessing - handles meta-information like <code>#include</code></li>
<li>Compiling - translates C++ into machine code objects</li>
<li>Linking - merges object into a single application</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-key-c-concepts" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#key-c-concepts"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Key C++ Concepts</h3>
<h4><a id="user-content-type" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#type"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Type</h4>
<ul>
<li>Type is a set of values and a set of operations</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Primitive types:
<ul>
<li>Built-in types: bool, char, int, float, void</li>
<li>Modifiers:
<ul>
<li>Signedness: signed, unsigned</li>
<li>Size: short, long, long long</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Constructing new types using declarator operators
<ul>
<li>Pointer types: int*</li>
<li>References: double&amp;</li>
<li>Array types: char[]</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>User-defined types:
<ul>
<li>The containers such as vector</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<h5><a id="user-content-implementation-defined-limits" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#implementation-defined-limits"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Implementation-defined <code>&lt;limits&gt;</code></h5>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>iostream<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>
#<span class="pl-k">include</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">&lt;</span>limits<span class="pl-pds">&gt;</span></span>

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>() {
  std::cout &lt;&lt; std::numeric_limits&lt;<span class="pl-k">double</span>&gt;::<span class="pl-c1">max</span>() &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
  std::cout &lt;&lt; std::numeric_limits&lt;<span class="pl-k">double</span>&gt;::<span class="pl-c1">min</span>() &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
  std::cout &lt;&lt; std::numeric_limits&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt;::<span class="pl-c1">max</span>() &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
  std::cout &lt;&lt; std::numeric_limits&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt;::<span class="pl-c1">min</span>() &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> ...</span>
}</pre></div>
<h5><a id="user-content-deciding-which-types-to-use" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#deciding-which-types-to-use"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Deciding which types to use</h5>
<ul>
<li>Use <strong>unsigned</strong> for non-negative values</li>
<li>Use <strong>int</strong> for integer arithmetic</li>
<li>Use <strong>double</strong> for floating point computations</li>
<li>Use <strong>char</strong> or <strong>bool</strong> to hold characters or truth values</li>
<li><strong>void</strong>: a special type with no associated values or operations. It is most often used to specify empty return values for functions</li>
</ul>
<h5><a id="user-content-more-about-c" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#more-about-c"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>More (about C++)</h5>
<ul>
<li>Mixing signed and unsigned: signed is promoted to unsigned</li>
<li>Expression evaluation order
<ul>
<li>Order of evaluating the two operands of a binary operator is undefined (except for <code>&amp;&amp;</code>, <code>||</code>, and <code>,</code> (comma operator))</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">int</span> i = <span class="pl-c1">2</span>;
<span class="pl-k">int</span> j = (i = <span class="pl-c1">3</span>) * i;
std::cout &lt;&lt; j &lt;&lt; std::endl; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> 6 or 9</span>
a[i] + i++; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> undefined</span>
<span class="pl-en">foo</span>(a[i], i++); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> undefined</span>
<span class="pl-en">f</span>() + g(); <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> undefined</span></pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-declarations-vs-definitions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#declarations-vs-definitions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Declarations vs Definitions</h4>
<ul>
<li><strong>Declarations</strong>: makes known the type and the name of a variable
<ul>
<li>Introduces a name and its type into the program</li>
<li>Example
<ul>
<li><code>int getX(Point *p);</code></li>
<li><code>class stack;</code></li>
<li><code>template &lt;typename T&gt; class Node;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Definitions</strong>: is a declaration, but also allocates storage for, and possibly initialises, a variable
<ul>
<li>A definition defines the kind of entity a name refers to</li>
<li>Example
<ul>
<li><code>int error_no = 20;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>A variable must be defined exactly once and must be defined or declared before it is used</li>
<li><strong><code>extern</code></strong>: declares a variable without defining it, except when it is initialised</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-header-files" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#header-files"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Header Files</h4>
<ul>
<li>Header files are used to store rellated declarations and help us structure source code into multiple files</li>
<li>Header files allow us to make full use of C++'s support for separate compilation</li>
<li>Header files
<ul>
<li>Should contain only logically related declarations</li>
<li>Should generally not include definitions</li>
<li>May include class definitions, some <code>const</code> objects and inline functions</li>
<li>Should always be enclosed by header guards</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Header guards</strong>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>#<span class="pl-k">ifndef</span> MYHEADER_H
#<span class="pl-k">define</span> <span class="pl-en">MYHEADER_H</span>
...
#<span class="pl-k">endif</span></pre></div>
</li>
<li>Can not put variable definitions and function definitions in the header file</li>
<li><strong>One-Definition-Rule (ODR)</strong>
<ul>
<li>An entity has exactly one definition in a program</li>
<li>A header file can contain:
<ul>
<li>class declarations and definitions</li>
<li>template declarations and definitions</li>
<li>inline function definitions</li>
<li>variable (data) declarations</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Can not contain variable (data) and function definitions</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-pointers" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#pointers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Pointers</h4>
<ul>
<li>Pointers are variables that hold the address of an object</li>
<li>Allow indirect access to the objects they point to</li>
<li>A pointer has a type, a name, a value, and an address of its own</li>
<li>Obtain the address of an object by using <code>&amp;</code></li>
<li>Use <code>*</code>, the dereference operator to obtain the object a pointer points to (called <strong>pointee</strong>)</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-const" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#const"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a><code>const</code></h4>
<ul>
<li>Must be initialised when defined</li>
<li>The primary role of const is to specify immutability</li>
<li>Many objects don't have their values changed after initialisation
<ul>
<li>Like many function parameters are read but not written to</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>A const pointer is <code>* const</code> not <code>const *</code>
<ul>
<li><code>char *const cp1</code> -&gt; const pointer to a char</li>
<li><code>char const* cp2</code> -&gt; pointer to const char</li>
<li><code>const char* cp3</code> -&gt; pointer to const char</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Reference</strong>
<ul>
<li>C++ references are a way of aliasing objects</li>
<li><code>int &amp;r = i</code></li>
<li>Must be initialised when defined and may not be rebound to a new object</li>
<li>A reference is always <code>const</code> since it must be initialised when defined and cannot be modified later</li>
<li>A reference is not itself an object unlike a pointer which is an object</li>
<li>A reference to a const object is often said to be a const reference</li>
<li>A reference to a non-const object is often said to be a non-const reference</li>
<li>Reference is safer than pointers because they can never be null</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-auto" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#auto"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a><code>auto</code></h4>
<ul>
<li>The <code>auto</code> deduction: take exactly the type on the right-hand side but strip off the top-level const and &amp;. But the low-level const must be preserved</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Functions</h4>
<ul>
<li>Formal parameters are those that appear in the function definition, specifying the type and the name of each parameter</li>
<li>Actual parameters are those used when calling the function</li>
<li>A function must specify a return type, which maybe <code>void</code></li>
<li>A function may have an empty parameter list
<ul>
<li>Implicit void parameter list:
<ul>
<li><code>int foo();</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Explicit void parameter list:
<ul>
<li><code>void bar(void)</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Call by value</strong>
<ul>
<li>The actual argument is copied into a location being used to hold the formal parameter's value during method/function execution</li>
<li>rvalue</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Call by reference</strong>
<ul>
<li>The formal parameter just acts as an alias for the actual parameter.</li>
<li>The method/function is actually using the actual parameter whenever it uses the formal parameter</li>
<li>lvalue</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Parameter passing</strong>
<ul>
<li>Passing by value is not a good idea when:
<ul>
<li>the function changes the value of the argument</li>
<li>the argument is a large object</li>
<li>the parameter type has no copy operation</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Return values: functions may return pointers or references but make sure these are not to local objects</li>
</ul>
<h5><a id="user-content-function-overloading" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-overloading"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Function Overloading</h5>
<ul>
<li>Family of functions, in the same scope, with the same name, but different formal parameters</li>
<li>Overload resolution: the process by which the compiler chooses the correct version of an overloaded function for execution
<ol>
<li>Identify the <strong>candidate</strong> functions</li>
<li>Selecting the <strong>viable</strong> functions</li>
<li>Finding a <strong>best-match</strong></li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>If fails will produce a compile-time error</li>
</ul>
<h5><a id="user-content-inline-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#inline-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Inline Functions</h5>
<ul>
<li>Inline functions are expanded "in line" at each point in the program in which it is invoked</li>
<li>So the compiler must have access to the function definition in the header file in order to expand</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="user-content-week-2" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#week-2"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Week 2</h2>
<h3><a id="user-content-scope" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#scope"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Scope</h3>
<ul>
<li>The part of a program where a name is valid</li>
<li>5 scopes:
<ol>
<li>Local (blocks/compound statements delimited by {})</li>
<li>Function prototype (each parameter list is distinct)</li>
<li>Function (only applies to goto labels)</li>
<li>Namespace</li>
<li>Class scope</li>
</ol>
</li>
<li>A scope starts from its point of declaration</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-namespaces" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#namespaces"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Namespaces</h3>
<ul>
<li>Namespace scope: part of program for packaging names</li>
<li>To avoid name clashes with multiple, independently developed libraries</li>
<li><strong>Global scope</strong>: the outermost namespace scope of a file</li>
<li><strong>File scope</strong>: the namespace scope in a file (unnamed)
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">namespace</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> i = <span class="pl-c1">3</span>;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li><strong>using directive</strong>: makes the namespace members visible as if they were declared outside the namespace at the location where the namespace definition is located
<ul>
<li><code>using namespace std;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>using declaration</strong>: introduce a name into the scope where using declaration appears
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>std::cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>hello<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;
<span class="pl-k">using</span> std::cout;
cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>there<span class="pl-cce">\n</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>;</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Namespace clashes
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">namespace</span> <span class="pl-en">X</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> i, j, k;
};

<span class="pl-k">int</span> k;

<span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">main</span>() {
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> i = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;
  X::i; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> error: i declared twice</span>
  <span class="pl-k">using</span> X::j;
  <span class="pl-k">using</span> X::k; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> hides the global k</span>
  j++; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> X::j</span>
  k++; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> X::k</span>
}</pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-io" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#io"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>I/O</h3>
<ul>
<li>Predefined stream objects
<ul>
<li><code>cin</code> - standard input</li>
<li><code>cout</code> - standard output</li>
<li><code>cerr</code> - standard error</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Formatting
<ul>
<li><code>std::cout &lt;&lt; "In hex " &lt;&lt; std::hex &lt;&lt; 1331 &lt;&lt; std::endl;</code> - will print in hex</li>
<li><code>std::cout &lt;&lt; std::setprecision(3) &lt;&lt; 1331.123456 &lt;&lt; std::endl;</code> - print 3 d.p.</li>
<li>etc.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-strings" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#strings"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Strings</h3>
<ul>
<li>Use iterator and [] for speed</li>
<li>Use <code>at()</code> when you need range checking</li>
<li>Use <code>find()</code> operations to locate valules in a string</li>
<li>Use <code>isalpha()</code>, <code>isdigit()</code> for character classification</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-type-casting" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#type-casting"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Type Casting</h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>Objects</strong>
<ul>
<li>An object is a region of memory with a type</li>
<li>Two kinds of objects: class object and non-class object</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Strong Static Typing</strong>:  type-checking happens during compilation. Compiler will produce type-mismatch errors if types are used illegally. Types must be known at compile time.</li>
<li><strong>Type conversion</strong>
<ul>
<li><code>int b = true;</code> - a bool converted to an int</li>
<li><code>int pi = 3.14;</code> - pi has value of 3, no compiler warning</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Static casting</strong>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">double</span> myDouble = <span class="pl-c1">3.14</span>;
<span class="pl-k">int</span> cast = <span class="pl-k">static_cast</span>&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt;(myDouble);</pre></div>
</li>
<li><code>reinterpret_cast</code>: low level reinterpretation of the bit pattern
<ul>
<li>reat the sequence of bits (object representation) of expression as if it had the type new_type (from cppreference)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>const_cast</code>: removes low level const
<ul>
<li>Avoid if you can</li>
<li>Used mostly for portability</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-arrays" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#arrays"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Arrays</h3>
<ul>
<li>Use <code>vector</code> and <code>list</code> containers in STL
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>std::array&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>, <span class="pl-c1">4</span>&gt; a = {<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-c1">3</span>};</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Array is an indexed data structure, holds items of a single type, has a fixed size, sized at compile time, can't hold reference types, cannot be copied or assigned</li>
<li>It's better to use vector than array</li>
<li>Range-Based for in C++11
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>std::string <span class="pl-en">s</span>(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>Hello world!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>);
<span class="pl-k">for</span> (<span class="pl-k">auto</span> &amp;c: s) {
  c = <span class="pl-c1">std::toupper</span>(c);
}</pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-stl" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#stl"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>STL</h3>
<h4><a id="user-content-function-templates" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-templates"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Function Templates</h4>
<ul>
<li>A function template is a prescription for the compiler to generate a particular instances of a function varying by type</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">template </span>&lt;<span class="pl-k">typename</span> T&gt;
T <span class="pl-en">min</span>(T a, T b) {
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> a &lt; b ? a : b;
}</pre></div>
<h4><a id="user-content-c-stl" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#c-stl"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>C++ STL</h4>
<ul>
<li>All components of the STL are templates</li>
<li>Containers are copyable/movable/assignable</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-sequential-containers" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#sequential-containers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Sequential Containers</h3>
<h4><a id="user-content-vector" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#vector"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Vector</h4>
<ul>
<li>Most commonly used container</li>
<li>Fast random access to element</li>
<li>Insertion and removal of elements at the end is fast</li>
<li>Insertion and removal elsewhere in the vector may be very slow</li>
<li>Type must have default constructor</li>
<li>[] at invalid index is undefined</li>
<li><code>size()</code> - how many elements the vector has</li>
<li><code>capacity()</code> - the number of elements the vector can hold</li>
<li><code>assign</code>
<ul>
<li>For different types, but type must be type-assignable</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-other-sequential-containers" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#other-sequential-containers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Other Sequential Containers</h4>
<ul>
<li><code>std::list</code>
<ul>
<li>Implemented as a doubly-linked list</li>
<li>No method for random access</li>
<li>Support for fast merging and splicing of lists</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>std::forward_list</code>
<ul>
<li>A singly-linked list with pointers from each node only to the next one</li>
<li>Takes less memory</li>
<li>No -- for iterators</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>std::deque</code>
<ul>
<li>Like vector but allows fast insertion and removal from its beginning as well</li>
<li>Using <code>push_front()</code> and <code>pop_front()</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>std::array</code>
<ul>
<li>Constant-size array</li>
<li>Size must be known at compile time</li>
<li>Basically wraps a C-style array inside</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Adaptors: <code>stack</code>, <code>queue</code>, and <code>priority_queue</code>
<ul>
<li>Defines them as adaptors built from a basic sequence type, but with the API that we really want</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-associative-containers" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#associative-containers"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Associative Containers</h3>
<ul>
<li>A <strong>value type</strong> is accessed through a second data type, the <strong>key</strong></li>
<li>The elements are either unordered or ordered based on their key values rather than the order of insertion</li>
<li>by default, <code>operator&lt;</code> is used to compare the keys</li>
<li><code>set</code>
<ul>
<li>The value type and key are the same</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>map</code>
<ul>
<li>A collection of pairs</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-iterators" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#iterators"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Iterators</h3>
<ul>
<li>Iterator is an abstract notion of pointers</li>
<li>Glue between containers and generic algorithms</li>
<li><code>a.begin()</code>: a pointer to the first element</li>
<li><code>a.end()</code>: a pointer to one past the last element</li>
<li>If <code>p</code> points to the k-th element
<ul>
<li><code>*p</code> is the object pointed to</li>
<li><code>++p</code> points to (k+1)-th element</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Every iterator declared is non-const, so that it can be used to iterate through the elements in a container</li>
<li>A const iterator for a container is an iterator that "points" to a const element in the container
<ul>
<li>This can not be used to modify the container elements</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Non const - can be used to modify the container elements</li>
<li><strong>Reverse iterators</strong>
<ul>
<li><code>first</code>: pointer to last element</li>
<li><code>last</code>: pointer to element before the 1st element</li>
<li><code>++p</code> points to (k-1)-th element</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-categories" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#categories"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Categories</h4>
<ul>
<li>Input: read, access, ++, ==, !=</li>
<li>Output: write, ++</li>
<li>Forward: read, access, write, ++, ==, !=</li>
<li>Bidirectional: read, access, write, ++, --, ==, !=</li>
<li>Random: read, access (also []), write, ++, --, +, -, +=, -=, ==, !=, &lt;, &gt;, &gt;=, &lt;=</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="user-content-week-3" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#week-3"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Week 3</h2>
<h3><a id="user-content-object-oriented-programming" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#object-oriented-programming"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Object Oriented Programming</h3>
<ul>
<li>A class uses data abstraction and encapsulation to define an abstract data type</li>
<li><strong>Interface</strong>: the oprationsn used by the user</li>
<li><strong>Implementation</strong>: the data members, the bodies of the functions in the interface and any other function not intended for general use</li>
<li><strong>Abstraction</strong>: separation of interface from implementation</li>
<li><strong>Encapsulation</strong>: enforcement of this via information hiding</li>
<li>Member access control: can be <code>public</code> or <code>private</code></li>
<li>Class scope: needs the class name and <code>::</code> if definiton outside the class header thing</li>
<li><code>this</code> pointer: member function has an extra implicit parameter, a pointer to the object on behalf of which the function is called.</li>
<li>returning the object: <code>return *this;</code></li>
<li>Overloading based on <code>const</code>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp; <span class="pl-en">Sales_data::print</span>(ostream &amp;os) <span class="pl-k">const</span>
Sales_data&amp; Sales_data::print(ostream &amp;os)</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Mutable data members: can be modified if the object is a const object
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">mutable</span> <span class="pl-k">unsigned</span> num_called = <span class="pl-c1">0</span>;</pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-constructors" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#constructors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Constructors</h3>
<ul>
<li>Define how class data members are intialised</li>
<li>Has the same name as the class and no return type</li>
<li>The compiler generated default constructor
<pre><code>for each data member in declaration order
  if it has an in-class initialiser
    Initialise it using the in-class initialiser
  else
    if it is of a built-in type
    it is undefined // local scope
    else
      Initialise it using its default constructor
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-constructor-initializer-list" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#constructor-initializer-list"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Constructor Initializer List</h4>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">A</span> {
<span class="pl-k">public:</span>
  <span class="pl-en">A</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> i, <span class="pl-k">int</span> j): j{i}, i{j}{}
<span class="pl-k">private:</span>
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> j;
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> i;
};</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>The order is important! In the order variables are declared</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-delegating-constructors" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#delegating-constructors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Delegating Constructors</h4>
<ul>
<li>A constructor can call another constructor</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-en">Sales_data</span>(<span class="pl-k">const</span> std::string &amp;s, <span class="pl-k">unsigned</span> n, <span class="pl-k">double</span> p):
            bookNo{s}, units_sold{n}, revenue{p*n} { }

<span class="pl-en">Sales_data</span>() : Sales_data{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span><span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">0</span>} { }

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Sales_data(const std::string &amp;s): bookName{s} { }</span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> replace with:</span>
<span class="pl-en">Sales_data</span>(<span class="pl-k">const</span> std::string &amp;s) : Sales_data{s, <span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">0</span>} { }

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> tell this constructor to call the default constructor first</span>
<span class="pl-en">Sales_data</span>(std::istream &amp;is) : Sales_data{} {
  <span class="pl-c1">read</span>(is, *<span class="pl-c1">this</span>);
}</pre></div>
<h3><a id="user-content-uniform-initialisation" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#uniform-initialisation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Uniform initialisation</h3>
<ul>
<li>"If it can possiblly be interpreted as a function prototype, then it will be"</li>
<li>Solution: use {} instead of () because it can't be mistaken for function calls</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-friends" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#friends"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Friends</h3>
<ul>
<li>A friend of a class can access its private members</li>
<li>A class makes a function its friend by including a declaration for that function preceeded by the keyword <code>friend</code></li>
<li>3 types of friends:
<ul>
<li>An ordinary function
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Sales_data</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">friend</span> std::ostream&amp; <span class="pl-en">print</span>(std::ostream&amp;, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp;);
};</pre></div>
</li>
<li>A class
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Screen</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">friend</span> <span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Window_Mgr</span>;
};</pre></div>
</li>
<li>A member function of a class
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Screen2</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">friend</span> Window_Mgr&amp; <span class="pl-en">Window_Mgr::relocate</span>(Screen&amp;);
};
</pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-type-conversions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#type-conversions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Type Conversions</h3>
<ul>
<li>Static data member
<ul>
<li>Contained in the class, not in the object</li>
<li>Objects only contain non-static data members</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Implicit Type Conversions
<ul>
<li>Constructors can create implicit conversions from other types to the class type</li>
<li>A constructor that can be called with a single argument defines an implicit conversion
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">Foo</span> {
<span class="pl-k">public:</span>
  <span class="pl-en">Foo</span>(<span class="pl-k">const</span> std::vector&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt; v) : data{v} {}
<span class="pl-k">private:</span>
  std::vector&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt; data;
};

std::vector&lt;<span class="pl-k">int</span>&gt; ivec;
Foo foo = ivec; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> create a Foo object</span></pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><code>explicit</code> - suppressing implicit conversion
<ul>
<li><code>explicit Sales_data(std::istream&amp;);</code></li>
<li>To stop the implicit type conversions</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-copy-control" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#copy-control"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Copy Control</h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>Initialisation</strong>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>MyClass one;
MyClass two = one;</pre></div>
</li>
<li><strong>Assignment</strong>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>MyClass one, two;
two = one;</pre></div>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Special member functions:</p>
<ul>
<li>Move Constructor</li>
<li>Move Assignment</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-copy-assignment" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#copy-assignment"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Copy Assignment</h4>
<ul>
<li>Takes only one argument of the same type</li>
<li>Returns a reference to its left-hand operand</li>
<li><code>A&amp; operator=(const A &amp;a) { ... }</code></li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-copy-constructor" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#copy-constructor"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Copy Constructor</h4>
<ul>
<li>A constructor is the copy ctor if its first parameter is a reference to the class type and any additional parameters have default values
<ul>
<li><code>A (const A &amp;a) { ... }</code></li>
<li>Copy initialisation is like
<ul>
<li><code>MyString s2 = "abc";</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-destructors" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#destructors"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Destructors</h4>
<ul>
<li>Unique, can not be overloaded</li>
<li>2 things happen when called:
<ul>
<li>The function body of the destructor is executed</li>
<li>The members are destryoed by calling their destructors in their reverse declaration order</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>This is the process of object construction in reverse</li>
<li>Members of STL container types or smart pointers are automatically destroyed</li>
<li>Used to free memory allocated via <code>new</code> or some other resources</li>
<li>No need to provide a destructor if its data member are of non-pointer-related built-in types</li>
<li>Destructors are called when the variable go out of scope</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-preventing-copies" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#preventing-copies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Preventing Copies</h4>
<p><code>NoCopy(const NoCopy &amp;data) = delete;</code></p>
<ul>
<li><code>= delete</code> tells the compiler not to generate this member</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="user-content-week-4" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#week-4"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Week 4</h2>
<h3><a id="user-content-copy-control-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#copy-control-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Copy Control</h3>
<ul>
<li>Compiler generated copy constructor and assignment are shallow copy</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-move-semantics" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#move-semantics"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Move Semantics</h4>
<ul>
<li>To avoid unnecessary copies when working with temporary objects that are about to evaporate, and whole resources can safely be taken from that such a temporary object and used by another</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-general-strategies-for-classes" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#general-strategies-for-classes"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>General Strategies for Classes</h4>
<ul>
<li>Value-like classes
<ul>
<li>Class data members have their own state</li>
<li>When an object is copied, the copy and the original are independent of each other</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Pointer-like classes
<ul>
<li>Class data members share state</li>
<li>When an object is copied, the copy and the original use the same underlying data</li>
<li>Changes made to the copy also affect the original, and vice versa</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-noexcept" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#noexcept"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a><code>noexcept</code></h3>
<ul>
<li>Signals to the compiler and optimiser that no exception will be thrown from the method</li>
<li>Automatically provided for compiler synthesised big five</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-lvalues-and-rvalues" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#lvalues-and-rvalues"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Lvalues and Rvalues</h3>
<ul>
<li><strong>Lvalues</strong>: an object's identity or address</li>
<li><strong>Rvalues</strong>: an object's value</li>
<li><strong>Lvalue reference</strong>: formed by placing <code>&amp;</code> after some type
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>A a;
A&amp; a_ref1 = a;</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>Functions that return lvalue ref: <code>++i</code>, <code>*p</code>, <code>a[2]</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><strong>Rvalue reference</strong>: formed by placing <code>&amp;&amp;</code> after some type
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>A a;
A&amp;&amp; a_ref2 = a;</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>Functions that return rvalue ref: <code>i++</code>, <code>i + j</code>, <code>i &lt; k</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-argument-dependent-lookup" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#argument-dependent-lookup"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Argument Dependent Lookup</h3>
<ul>
<li>First the normal name lookup for f is performed</li>
<li>Then, look for f in the namespace scope where x is defined</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-operator-overloading" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#operator-overloading"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Operator Overloading</h3>
<h4><a id="user-content-rules-and-exceptions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#rules-and-exceptions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Rules and Exceptions</h4>
<ul>
<li>Overload operators must have at least one operand of class or enumeration type</li>
<li><code>,</code>, <code>&amp;</code>, <code>&amp;&amp;</code>, <code>||</code> should usually not be overloaded</li>
<li>Usually when we make a class need to overload the subscript, call, access arrow. Also need to define some operator as friend functions (eg. <code>&lt;&lt;</code> and <code>&gt;&gt;</code>)</li>
</ul>
<h4><a id="user-content-overloading-example" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#overloading-example"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Overloading Example</h4>
<ul>
<li>I/O Operators
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>std::ostream&amp; <span class="pl-k">operator</span>&lt;&lt;(std::ostream &amp;os, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;item) {
  os &lt;&lt; item.<span class="pl-c1">isbn</span>() &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span> <span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; item.<span class="pl-smi">units_sold</span> &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span> <span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>
  &lt;&lt; item.<span class="pl-smi">revenue</span> &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span> <span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; item.<span class="pl-c1">avg_price</span>();
<span class="pl-k">return</span> os;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Compound Assignment Operators
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>Sales_data&amp; Sales_data::<span class="pl-k">operator</span>+=(<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;rhs) {
  units_sold += rhs.<span class="pl-smi">units_sold</span>;
  revenue += rhs.<span class="pl-smi">revenue</span>;
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> *<span class="pl-c1">this</span>;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Arithmetic
<ul>
<li>Usually non member functions</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>Sales_data <span class="pl-k">operator</span>+(<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;lhs, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;rhs) {
  Sales_data sum = lhs;
  sum += rhs;
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> sum;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Relational operators
<ul>
<li>Usually non member functions</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>Sales_data.h:
<span class="pl-k">friend</span> <span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-k">operator</span>== (<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp;, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp;);
<span class="pl-k">friend</span> <span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-k">operator</span>!=(<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp;, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data&amp;);

Sales_data.cpp:
<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-k">operator</span>==(<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;lhs, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;rhs) {
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> lhs.<span class="pl-c1">isbn</span>() == rhs.<span class="pl-c1">isbn</span>() &amp;&amp;
      lhs.<span class="pl-smi">units_sold</span> == rhs.<span class="pl-smi">units_sold</span> &amp;&amp;
      lhs.<span class="pl-smi">revenue</span> == rhs.<span class="pl-smi">revenue</span>;
}

<span class="pl-k">bool</span> <span class="pl-k">operator</span>!=(<span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;lhs, <span class="pl-k">const</span> Sales_data &amp;rhs) {
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> !(lhs == rhs);
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Subscript Operator <code>[]</code>
<ul>
<li>setting: <code>int&amp; operator[](int i);</code></li>
<li>getting: <code>int operator[](int i) const;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Increment and decrement operators
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> prefix</span>
Clock &amp; Clock::<span class="pl-k">operator</span>++() {
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> increment</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">tick</span>();
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> return itself for assignment</span>
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> *<span class="pl-c1">this</span>;
}

Clock Clock::<span class="pl-k">operator</span>++(<span class="pl-k">int</span>) { <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> postfix</span>
  Clock c = *<span class="pl-c1">this</span>; <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">/*</span> Save/copy the object<span class="pl-c">*/</span></span>
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Increment the object</span>
  <span class="pl-c1">tick</span>();
  <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> Return the original object</span>
  <span class="pl-k">return</span> c;
}</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>pre inc: lvalues, returns a reference</li>
<li>post inc: rvalues, return a value, it does more work</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Arrow and dereferencing operators
<ul>
<li>-&gt; and * are overloaded to provide pointer-like behaviour</li>
<li>Must be member function</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Type Conversion Operators
<ul>
<li>Two-way user-defined conversions when defining a new class</li>
<li>Single-arg constructors: old types to the new type</li>
<li>The new type to some old types:
<ul>
<li><code>operator type() const;</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Must be defined as member functions, don't take any parameters, and don't specify a return type</li>
<li>Typically conversions don't modify the object so declared <code>const</code></li>
<li>Can also be <code>explicit</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-callable-objects" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#callable-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Callable Objects</h3>
<h4><a id="user-content-the-call-operator" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-call-operator"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>The Call Operator()</h4>
<ul>
<li>Must be defined as a member function</li>
<li>Can be overloaded in a class to create a so-called <strong>function object</strong> or <strong>functor</strong>, an object that can act as a function</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">struct</span> <span class="pl-en">AbsInt</span> {
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> <span class="pl-en">operator</span>() (<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-k">int</span> val) <span class="pl-k">const</span> {
    <span class="pl-k">return</span> (val &lt; <span class="pl-c1">0</span>) ? -val : val;
  }
};</pre></div>
<h4><a id="user-content-structure-of-stl-algorithms" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#structure-of-stl-algorithms"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Structure of STL Algorithms</h4>
<ul>
<li>Most STL algorithms take one of these forms:</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-en">std::alg</span>(beg, end, other args);
<span class="pl-en">std::alg</span>(beg, end, dest, other args);
<span class="pl-en">std::alg</span>(beg, end, beg2, other args);
<span class="pl-en">std::alg</span>(beg, end, beg2, end2, other args);</pre></div>
<h4><a id="user-content-callable-objects-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#callable-objects-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Callable Objects</h4>
<ul>
<li>5 kinds of callable objects
<ul>
<li>Functions</li>
<li>Pointers to functions</li>
<li>Objects of a class that overloads ()</li>
<li>Objects created by <strong>bind</strong></li>
<li>Objects created by <strong>lambda expressions</strong></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-bind-objects" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#bind-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Bind objects</h3>
<ul>
<li>A general-purpose function adaptor</li>
<li>Takes a callable object and generates a new one that adapts the parameter list of the original object
<ul>
<li><code>auto newCallable = std::bind(Callable, arg_list);</code></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h3><a id="user-content-lambda-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#lambda-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Lambda Functions</h3>
<ul>
<li>Can be considered as an unnamed, inline function</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>[capture list] (parameter list) -&gt; <span class="pl-k">return</span> type {
  function body
}</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>Capture list: a list of local variables available in the enclosing function</li>
<li>Parameter list and return type can be omitted</li>
<li>Can store a lambda function into a named type</li>
<li>Passing arguments to a lambda</li>
</ul>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-en">std::stable_sort</span>(words.begin(), words.end(),
                [](<span class="pl-k">const</span> std::string &amp;s1, <span class="pl-k">const</span> std::string &amp;s2) {
                  <span class="pl-k">return</span> s1.<span class="pl-c1">size</span>() &lt; s2.<span class="pl-c1">size</span>();
                });</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>Lambda captures
<ul>
<li><code>[v1]</code> - capture the value</li>
<li><code>[&amp;v1]</code> - capture the reference</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Implicit captures
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> os implicitly captured by reference</span>
<span class="pl-en">std::for_each</span>(wc, words.end(),
              [&amp;, c](<span class="pl-k">const</span> string &amp;s) {
                os &lt;&lt; s &lt;&lt; c;
              });

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">//</span> c implicitly captured by value</span>
<span class="pl-en">std::for_each</span>(wc, words.end(),
              [=, &amp;os](<span class="pl-k">const</span> string &amp;s) {
                os &lt;&lt; s &lt;&lt; c;
              });</pre></div>
<ul>
<li>if the first is
<ul>
<li><code>=</code> - the explicitly captured variables must be captured by reference</li>
<li><code>&amp;</code> - the explicitly captured variables must be captured by value</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Return type
<ul>
<li>Must specify return type when it cannot be reduced</li>
<li>Typically deduced when there is a single return statement</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2><a id="user-content-week-5" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#week-5"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Week 5</h2>
<h3><a id="user-content-exception-handling" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#exception-handling"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Exception Handling</h3>
<ul>
<li>Exceptions: run-time anomalies</li>
<li>Exception-handling: a run-time mechanism to communicate exceptions between two unrelated parts</li>
<li>In C++: <code>throw 100;</code></li>
<li><code>#include &lt;stdexcept&gt;</code></li>
<li>Example of exception class
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">class</span> <span class="pl-en">bad_push</span> {
<span class="pl-k">public:</span>
  <span class="pl-en">bad_push</span>(<span class="pl-k">int</span> idx) : index {idx} { }
  <span class="pl-en">value</span>() { <span class="pl-k">return</span> <span class="pl-c1">index</span>; }
<span class="pl-k">private:</span>
  <span class="pl-k">int</span> index;
};</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Using it
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre><span class="pl-k">void</span> <span class="pl-en">Stack::push</span>(<span class="pl-k">const</span> <span class="pl-k">int</span> &amp;item) {
  <span class="pl-k">if</span> (<span class="pl-c1">full</span>()) <span class="pl-k">throw</span> bad_push{currentIndex};
  stack_[++top_] = item;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Try-catch block
<div class="highlight highlight-source-c++"><pre>Stack s{<span class="pl-c1">2</span>};
<span class="pl-k">try</span> {
  s.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>);
  s.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>);
  s.<span class="pl-c1">push</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3</span>);
} <span class="pl-k">catch</span> (bad_push &amp;e) {
  cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>bab_push: index=<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; e.<span class="pl-c1">value</span>() &lt;&lt; endl;
} <span class="pl-k">catch</span> (bad_pop) {
  cout &lt;&lt; <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>bab_pop caught!<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> &lt;&lt; endl;
}</pre></div>
</li>
<li>Catch exceptions by <code>const&amp;</code> if possible
<ul>
<li>Object thrown is always copied</li>
<li>Should not catch by pointer because ownership</li>
<li>Problems with catch by value: inefficient due to object copying, causes the slicing problem, cannot exploit polymorphism and dynamic binding</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Rethrow
<ul>
<li>just do <code>throw;</code> inside the catch block</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
